</div>
			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Drama Series</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with the <a href="/wiki/Daytime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Drama_Series" title="Daytime Emmy Award for Outstanding Drama Series">Daytime Emmy Award with the same name</a>.</div>
<table class="infobox vevent" style="width:22em">
<tr>
<th colspan="2" class="summary" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background-color: #eedd82;"><a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award" title="Primetime Emmy Award">Primetime Emmy Award</a> for Outstanding Drama Series</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">Awarded for</th>
<td>Outstanding Drama Series</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">Country</th>
<td class="location"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">Presented by</th>
<td class="attendee"><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Television_Arts_%26_Sciences" title="Academy of Television Arts &amp; Sciences">Academy of Television Arts &amp; Sciences</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">First awarded</th>
<td>1951</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">Currently held by</th>
<td><i><a href="/wiki/The_Handmaid%27s_Tale" title="The Handmaid's Tale">The Handmaid's Tale</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/69th_Primetime_Emmy_Awards" title="69th Primetime Emmy Awards">2017</a>)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">Website</th>
<td><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://emmys.com">emmys<wbr />.com</a></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>This is a list of winners and nominees of the <b><a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award" title="Primetime Emmy Award">Primetime Emmy Award</a> for Outstanding Drama Series</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> since its institution in 1951. The award is often cited as one of the "main awards" at the Emmys ceremonies,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> and has changed names many times in its history. It was first called <b>Best Dramatic Show</b> from 1951 to 1954, then <b>Best Dramatic Series</b> in 1955 and 1956. In 1957, no specific award for drama was given, but in 1958 the category was split into two separate categories, <b>Best Dramatic Anthology Series</b>, and <b>Best Dramatic Series with Continuing Characters</b> with a winner selected from each category. The following year, the category was differently split into two separate categories, <b>Best Dramatic Series – Less Than One Hour</b>. In 1960, the name was changed yet again to <b>Outstanding Program Achievement in the Field of Drama</b>; this name was kept from 1960 to 1964. In 1966, it had its sixth name change to <b>Outstanding Dramatic Series or Outstanding Series-Drama</b>; this was used from 1966 until recently, when it became <b>Outstanding Drama Series</b>.</p>
<p>In 1988, <i><a href="/wiki/Rumpole_of_the_Bailey" title="Rumpole of the Bailey">Rumpole of the Bailey</a></i> (PBS) was initially nominated in the <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Limited_Series" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Limited Series">Outstanding Miniseries</a> category<sup id="cite_ref-lat-1988jul29_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat-1988jul29-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ct-1988jul29_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ct-1988jul29-4">[4]</a></sup> but the Academy ruled that the nomination was not valid a few days later<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> and later allowed the program to compete in the <b>Outstanding Drama Series</b> category.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since 2000, every single winner has been a <a href="/wiki/Serial_(radio_and_television)" title="Serial (radio and television)">serial drama</a>: <i><a href="/wiki/The_West_Wing" title="The West Wing">The West Wing</a></i> (2000–2003), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sopranos" title="The Sopranos">The Sopranos</a></i> (2004, 2007), <i><a href="/wiki/Lost_(TV_series)" title="Lost (TV series)">Lost</a></i> (2005), <i><a href="/wiki/24_(TV_series)" title="24 (TV series)">24</a></i> (2006), <i><a href="/wiki/Mad_Men" title="Mad Men">Mad Men</a></i> (2008–2011), <i><a href="/wiki/Homeland_(TV_series)" title="Homeland (TV series)">Homeland</a></i> (2012), <i><a href="/wiki/Breaking_Bad" title="Breaking Bad">Breaking Bad</a></i> (2013–2014), <i><a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones" title="Game of Thrones">Game of Thrones</a></i> (2015–2016), and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Handmaid%27s_Tale_(TV_series)" title="The Handmaid's Tale (TV series)">The Handmaid's Tale</a></i> (2017). Since the advent of <i><a href="/wiki/Hill_Street_Blues" title="Hill Street Blues">Hill Street Blues</a></i> in 1981, every winner has had some <a href="/wiki/Story_arc" title="Story arc">serialized arcs</a> with the exception of <i><a href="/wiki/Law_%26_Order" title="Law &amp; Order">Law &amp; Order</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="ref_lawAndOrder"><a href="#endnote_lawAndOrder">[A]</a></sup> The majority of these shows have won between their first and fifth seasons. Only two shows have won on their sixth season, <i><a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones" title="Game of Thrones">Game of Thrones</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sopranos" title="The Sopranos">The Sopranos</a></i>, and only one on its seventh, <i><a href="/wiki/Law_%26_Order" title="Law &amp; Order">Law &amp; Order</a></i>.</p>
<p></p>

<td colspan="3">In 1988, <i>Rumpole of the Bailey</i> was added to this category after it was nominated and disqualified in the Miniseries category. As of March 2017<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Drama_Series&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, both the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Television_Arts_%26_Sciences" title="Academy of Television Arts &amp; Sciences">Academy of Television Arts &amp; Sciences</a><sup id="cite_ref-atas1988_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atas1988-41">[41]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Internet_Movie_Database" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet Movie Database">Internet Movie Database</a><br />
<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> still incorrectly omit <i>Rumpole of the Bailey</i> as a nominee.</td>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Drama_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="refbegin refbegin-hanging-indents columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<dl>
<dd>A<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_lawAndOrder"></span>&#160;: Saying <i>Law &amp; Order</i> had no serialized arcs is potentially misleading. It's true that <i>Law &amp; Order</i> is at its core a procedural, with only <i>very</i> lightly-serialized elements as a general rule. However, in its Emmy-winning <a href="/wiki/Law_%26_Order_(season_7)" title="Law &amp; Order (season 7)">seventh season</a>, the show had a three-episode arc—"D-Girl", "Turnaround", and "Showtime"—concerning a high-profile murder case. In addition, the episode "Entrapment" was a sequel to <a href="/wiki/Law_%26_Order_(season_3)#Episodes" title="Law &amp; Order (season 3)">season 3's "Conspiracy"</a> .</dd>
<dd>B<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_theSopranos"></span>&#160;: The sixth season of <i>The Sopranos</i> was split into two parts. They are both considered season 6.</dd>
<dd>C<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_breakingBad"></span>&#160;: The fifth season of <i>Breaking Bad</i> was split into two parts. They are both considered season 5.</dd>
<dd>D<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_madMen"></span>&#160;: The seventh season of <i>Mad Men</i> was split into two parts. They are both considered season 7.</dd>
</dl>
</div>

<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Rosenberg, Howard (August 28, 1988). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://articles.latimes.com/1988-08-28/news/tv-1468_1_lead-comedy-series-actor">"A TV Critic Marks His Emmy Ballot"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">November 22,</span> 2014</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APrimetime+Emmy+Award+for+Outstanding+Drama+Series&amp;rft.atitle=A+TV+Critic+Marks+His+Emmy+Ballot&amp;rft.aufirst=Howard&amp;rft.aulast=Rosenberg&amp;rft.date=1988-08-28&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Los+Angeles+Times&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Farticles.latimes.com%2F1988-08-28%2Fnews%2Ftv-1468_1_lead-comedy-series-actor&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 1958, two separate drama series categories existed, Best Dramatic Series with Continuing Characters and Best Dramatic Anthology Series, and an award was given in each category. <i>Gunsmoke</i> won Best Dramatic Series with Continuing Characters, while <i>Playhouse 90</i> won Best Dramatic Anthology Series.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 1959, two separate drama series categories existed, Best Dramatic Series-Less Than One Hour and Best Dramatic Series-One Hour or Longer, and an award was given in each category. <i>Alcoa-Goodyear Theatre</i> won Best Dramatic Series-Less Than One Hour, while <i>Playhouse 90</i> won Best Dramatic Series-One Hour or Longer.</span></li>

<th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="background: #EEDD82;;width:1%">Performance</th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-even hlist" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Lead_Actor_in_a_Comedy_Series" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Lead Actor in a Comedy Series">Lead Actor in a Comedy Series</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Lead_Actor_in_a_Limited_Series_or_Movie" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Lead Actor in a Limited Series or Movie">Lead Actor in a Limited Series or Movie</a></li>
